# Benchmark Report (MCP): agieval_lsat - lsat_42

**Provider:** openrouter5
**Model:** deepseek/deepseek-v4-flash
**Solver:** z3
**Config:** max_output_tokens: 32768, temperature: 0.0, top_p: 1.0, seed: 42, reasoning_enabled: False, reasoning_effort: none
**Duration:** 99.72s


 MCP Z3 AGENT - Symbolic Reasoning

### Query
A bakery makes exactly three kinds of cookie—oatmeal, peanut butter, and sugar. Exactly three

batches of each kind of cookie are made each week (Monday through Friday) and each batch is made,
from start to finish, on a single day. The following conditions apply: No two batches of the same
kind of cookie are made on the same day. At least one batch of cookies is made on Monday. The second
batch of oatmeal cookies is made on the same day as the first batch of peanut butter cookies. The
second batch of sugar cookies is made on Thursday.Q: If one kind of cookie's first batch is made on
the same day as another kind of cookie's third batch, then which one of the following could be
false? Answer Choices: (A)At least one batch of cookies is made on each of the five days. (B)At
least two batches of cookies are made on Wednesday. (C)Exactly one batch of cookies is made on
Monday. (D)Exactly two batches of cookies are made on Tuesday. (E)Exactly one batch of cookies is
made on Friday. A: Among A through E, the answer is

  - write_and_run_z3: Write Python code using Z3 to a file and run it immediately to get results.
We capture printed stdout and stderr from running the script.

## Iteration 1




### TOKEN USAGE - Iteration 1

  Input tokens:  6,924
  Output tokens: 1,173
  Total tokens:  8,097

### Tool Call: write_and_run_z3

  Args: {
  "filename": "bakery_cookies.py",
  "code": "from z3 import *\n\n# We have 3 kinds: Oatmeal (O), Peanut Butter (P), Sugar (S)\n# Each kind has 3 batches (1st, 2nd, 3rd)\n# Days: Monday=0, Tuesday=1, Wednesday=2, Thursday=3, Friday=4\n\nsolver = Solver()\n\n# Variables: day each batch is made\n# O[i], P[i], S[i] for i=0,1,2 (0=first batch, 1=second batch, 2=third batch)\nO = [Int(f'O_{i}') for i in range(3)]\nP = [Int(f'P_{i}') for i in range(3)]\nS = [Int(f'S_{i}') for i in range(3)]\n\nall_batches = O + P + S\n\n# Domain: each batch on Monday(0) through Friday(4)\nfor b in all_batches:\n    solver.add(b >= 0, b <= 4)\n\n# No two batches of the same kind on the same day\nsolver.add(Distinct(O))\nsolver.add(Distinct(P))\nsolver.add(Distinct(S))\n\n# At least one batch on Monday\nsolver.add(Or([b == 0 for b in all_batches]))\n\n# The second batch of oatmeal cookies is made on the same day as the first batch of peanut butter cookies\nsolver.add(O[1] == P[0])\n\n# The second batch of sugar cookies is made on Thursday (day 3)\nsolver.add(S[1] == 3)\n\n# Additional condition from the question:\n# \"If one kind of cookie's first batch is made on the same day as another kind of cookie's third batch\"\n# We need to find which option COULD BE FALSE given this condition.\n# So we add this condition as a constraint and then test each option.\n\n# Let's encode: There exist two distinct kinds (k1, k2) such that\n# first batch of k1 is on the same day as third batch of k2.\n# We'll use auxiliary variables.\n\n# We have 3 kinds. Let's index them: 0=O, 1=P, 2=S\n# first_batch[k] = day of first batch of kind k\n# third_batch[k] = day of third batch of kind k\nfirst_batch = [O[0], P[0], S[0]]\nthird_batch = [O[2], P[2], S[2]]\n\n# There exist distinct kinds i, j such that first_batch[i] == third_batch[j]\ncondition = Or([\n    And(i != j, first_batch[i] == third_batch[j])\n    for i in range(3) for j in range(3)\n])\nsolver.add(condition)\n\n# Now evaluate each option\n# Option A: At least one batch of cookies is made on each of the five days.\n# i.e., for each day d (0..4), there exists some batch on that day.\nopt_a_constr = And([Or([b == d for b in all_batches]) for d in range(5)])\n\n# Option B: At least two batches of cookies are made on Wednesday (day 2).\nopt_b_constr = Sum([If(b == 2, 1, 0) for b in all_batches]) >= 2\n\n# Option C: Exactly one batch of cookies is made on Monday (day 0).\nopt_c_constr = Sum([If(b == 0, 1, 0) for b in all_batches]) == 1\n\n# Option D: Exactly two batches of cookies are made on Tuesday (day 1).\nopt_d_constr = Sum([If(b == 1, 1, 0) for b in all_batches]) == 2\n\n# Option E: Exactly one batch of cookies is made on Friday (day 4).\nopt_e_constr = Sum([If(b == 4, 1, 0) for b in all_batches]) == 1\n\n# The question asks: which one COULD BE FALSE?\n# This means: given the condition holds, which option is NOT necessarily true?\n# So we need to find an option that is NOT forced to be true.\n# Equivalently: there exists a model where the condition holds AND the option is FALSE.\n# So we test each option's negation.\n\nfound_options = []\nfor letter, constr in [(\"A\", opt_a_constr), (\"B\", opt_b_constr), (\"C\", opt_c_constr), (\"D\", opt_d_constr), (\"E\", opt_e_constr)]:\n    solver.push()\n    solver.add(Not(constr))  # Could this option be false?\n    if solver.check() == sat:\n        found_options.append(letter)\n    solver.pop()\n\nif len(found_options) == 1:\n    print(\"STATUS: sat\")\n    print(f\"answer:{found_options[0]}\")\nelif len(found_options) > 1:\n    print(\"STATUS: unsat\")\n    print(f\"Refine: Multiple options found {found_options}\")\nelse:\n    print(\"STATUS: unsat\")\n    print(\"Refine: No options found\")\n"
}

Friday=4\n\nsolver = Solver()\n\n# Variables: day each batch is made\n# O[i], P[i], S[i] for i=0,1,2 (0=first batch, 1=second batch, 2=third batch)\nO = [Int(f'O_{i}') for i in range(3)]\nP = [Int(f'P_{i}') for i in range(3)]\nS = [Int(f'S_{i}') for i in range(3)]\n\nall_batches = O + P + S\n\n# Domain: each batch on Monday(0) through Friday(4)\nfor b in all_batches:\n    solver.add(b >= 0, b <= 4)\n\n# No two batches of the same kind on the same day\nsolver.add(Distinct(O))\nsolver.add(Distinct(P))\nsolver.add(Distinct(S))\n\n# At least one batch on Monday\nsolver.add(Or([b == 0 for batch\"\nfirst_batch = [O[0], P[0], S[0]]\nthird_batch = [O[2], P[2], S[2]]\n\ncondition = Or([\n    And(i != j, first_batch[i] == third_batch[j])\n    for i in range(3) for j in solver.assertions():\n    solver_copy.add(c)\n\ncount = 0\nwhile solver_copy.check() == sat and count < 5:\n    m = solver_copy.model()\n    print(f\"Model {count}:\")\n    print(f\"  O: {m[O[0]]}, {m[O[1]]}, {m[O[2]]}\")\n    print(f\"  P: {m[P[0]]}, {m[P[1]]}, {m[P[2]]}\")\n    print(f\"  S: {m[S[0]]}, {m[S[1]]}, {m[S[2]]}\")\n    \n    # Check each option\n    all_b = O + P + S\n    vals = [m.eval(b) for b in all_b]\n    \n    # A: at least one on each day\n    a_holds = all(any(v == d for v in vals) for d in range(5))\n    # B: at least two on Wednesday (day 2)\n    b_holds = sum(1 for v in vals if v == 2) >= 2\n    # C: exactly one on Monday (day 0)\n    c_holds = sum(1 for v in vals if v == 0) == 1\n    # D: exactly two on Tuesday (day 1)\n    d_holds = sum(1 for v in vals if v == 1) == 2\n    # E: exactly one on Friday (day 4)\n    e_holds = sum(1 for v in vals if v == 4) == 1\n    \n    print(f\"  A={a_holds}, B={b_holds}, C={c_holds}, D={d_holds}, E={e_holds}\")\n    \n    # Block this model\n    solver_copy.add(Or([b != m.eval(b) for b in all_b]))\n    count += 1\n\nprint()\n\n# Now let's think about the question differently.\n# \"If condition X holds, which could be false?\"\n# This means: among A-E, which one is NOT necessarily true when X holds?\n# So we need to find an option that CAN be false (i.e., its negation is satisfiable with X).\n\n# Let's test each option's negation more carefully.\n# The issue might be that ALL options can be false, meaning the condition is too weak.\n# Let's re-read: \"If one kind of cookie's first batch is made on the same day as another kind of cookie's third batch\"\n# This means: there exist two DIFFERENT kinds where first of one = third of another.\n\n# Let's test each option's negation individually\nprint(\"=== Testing each option's negation ===\")\nfor letter, name in [(\"A\", \"At least one batch on each day\"), \n                      (\"B\", \"At least two batches on Wednesday\"),\n                      (\"C\", \"Exactly one batch on Monday\"),\n                      (\"D\", \"Exactly two batches on Tuesday\"),\n                      (\"E\", \"Exactly one batch on Friday\")]:\n    s = Solver()\n    for c in solver.assertions():\n        s.add(c)\n    \n    if letter == \"A\":\n        s.add(Not(And([Or([b == d for b in all_batches]) for d in range(5)])))\n    elif letter == \"B\":\n        s.add(Not(Sum([If(b == 2, 1, 0) for b in all_batches]) >= 2))\n    elif letter == \"C\":\n        s.add(Not(Sum([If(b == 0, 1, 0) for b in all_batches]) == 1))\n    elif letter == \"D\":\n        s.add(Not(Sum([If(b == 1, 1, 0) for b in all_batches]) == 2))\n    elif letter == \"E\":\n        s.add(Not(Sum([If(b == 4, 1, 0) for b in all_batches]) == 1))\n    \n    res = s.check()\n    print(f\"Option {letter} ({name}) negation: {res}\")\n    if res == sat:\n        m = s.model()\n        print(f\"  O: {m[O[0]]}, {m[O[1]]}, {m[O[2]]}\")\n        print(f\"  P: {m[P[0]]}, {m[P[1]]}, {m[P[2]]}\")\n        print(f\"  S: {m[S[0]]}, {m[S[1]]}, {m[S[2]]}\")\n"
}

### Tool Call: write_and_run_z3

  Args: {
  "filename": "bakery_cookies3.py",
  "code": "from z3 import *\n\n# We have 3 kinds: Oatmeal (O), Peanut Butter (P), Sugar (S)\n# Each kind has 3 batches (1st, 2nd, 3rd)\n# Days: Monday=0, Tuesday=1, Wednesday=2, Thursday=3, Friday=4\n\n# The question: \"If one kind of cookie's first batch is made on the same day as another kind of cookie's third batch, then which one of the following could be false?\"\n# This means: given the condition holds, which option is NOT necessarily true?\n# i.e., which option CAN be false (its negation is satisfiable)?\n\n# Let's test each option: can it be false while the condition holds?\n\nO = [Int(f'O_{i}') for i in range(3)]\nP = [Int(f'P_{i}') for i in range(3)]\nS = [Int(f'S_{i}') for i in range(3)]\nall_batches = O + P + S\n\nfound_options = []\n\nfor letter in [\"A\", \"B\", \"C\", \"D\", \"E\"]:\n    s = Solver()\n    \n    # Domain\n    for b in all_batches:\n        s.add(b >= 0, b <= 4)\n    \n    # No two batches of same kind on same day\n    s.add(Distinct(O))\n    s.add(Distinct(P))\n    s.add(Distinct(S))\n    \n    # At least one batch on Monday\n    s.add(Or([b == 0 for b in all_batches]))\n    \n    # Second oatmeal = first peanut butter\n    s.add(O[1] == P[0])\n    \n    # Second sugar on Thursday (day 3)\n    s.add(S[1] == 3)\n    \n    # Condition: one kind's first batch = another kind's third batch\n    first_batch = [O[0], P[0], S[0]]\n    third_batch = [O[2], P[2], S[2]]\n    \n    condition = Or([\n        And(i != j, first_batch[i] == third_batch[j])\n        for i in range(3) for j in range(3)\n    ])\n    s.add(condition)\n    \n    # Add the NEGATION of the option (to see if it CAN be false)\n    if letter == \"A\":\n        # Negation of \"at least one batch on each day\"\n        s.add(Not(And([Or([b == d for b in all_batches]) for d in range(5)])))\n    elif letter == \"B\":\n        # Negation of \"at least two batches on Wednesday (day 2)\"\n        s.add(Sum([If(b == 2, 1, 0) for b in all_batches]) < 2)\n    elif letter == \"C\":\n        # Negation of \"exactly one batch on Monday (day 0)\"\n        s.add(Sum([If(b == 0, 1, 0) for b in all_batches]) != 1)\n    elif letter == \"D\":\n        # Negation of \"exactly two batches on Tuesday (day 1)\"\n        s.add(Sum([If(b == 1, 1, 0) for b in all_batches]) != 2)\n    elif letter == \"E\":\n        # Negation of \"exactly one batch on Friday (day 4)\"\n        s.add(Sum([If(b == 4, 1, 0) for b in all_batches]) != 1)\n    \n    res = s.check()\n    print(f\"Option {letter} negation: {res}\")\n    if res == sat:\n        found_options.append(letter)\n        m = s.model()\n        print(f\"  O: {m[O[0]]}, {m[O[1]]}, {m[O[2]]}\")\n        print(f\"  P: {m[P[0]]}, {m[P[1]]}, {m[P[2]]}\")\n        print(f\"  S: {m[S[0]]}, {m[S[1]]}, {m[S[2]]}\")\n\nprint(f\"\\nFound options (can be false): {found_options}\")\n\nif len(found_options) == 1:\n    print(\"STATUS: sat\")\n    print(f\"answer:{found_options[0]}\")\nelif len(found_options) > 1:\n    print(\"STATUS: unsat\")\n    print(f\"Refine: Multiple options found {found_options}\")\nelse:\n    print(\"STATUS: unsat\")\n    print(\"Refine: No options found\")\n"
}

### Tool Call: write_and_run_z3

  Args: {
  "filename": "bakery_cookies4.py",
  "code": "from z3 import *\n\n# Let me re-analyze the problem.\n# The question: \"If one kind of cookie's first batch is made on the same day as another kind of cookie's third batch, then which one of the following could be false?\"\n# \n# This is a conditional question: we assume the condition holds, and ask which option COULD be false.\n# \"Could be false\" means: under the given constraints + condition, the option is NOT necessarily true.\n# So we need to find which option has a SATISFIABLE negation under the constraints + condition.\n#\n# But wait - maybe I'm misunderstanding. Let me re-read.\n# \"If [condition], then which one of the following could be false?\"\n# This means: given the condition holds, which statement is NOT forced to be true?\n# So we check: under constraints + condition, is the negation of the option satisfiable?\n#\n# But all 5 options had sat negations. That means none of them are forced true.\n# That can't be right for an LSAT question. Let me re-think.\n#\n# Actually, maybe the condition \"one kind's first batch = another kind's third batch\" \n# is an additional constraint that we ADD to the scenario, and we need to see which \n# option could be false (i.e., is not necessarily true).\n#\n# Let me check: maybe some options are actually forced true, and my model is wrong.\n# Let me check each option's truth value more carefully.\n\n# Let me first check: under the base constraints + condition, what are the possible schedules?\n\nO = [Int(f'O_{i}') for i in range(3)]\nP = [Int(f'P_{i}') for i in range(3)]\nS = [Int(f'S_{i}') for i in range(3)]\nall_batches = O + P + S\n\ns = Solver()\nfor b in all_batches:\n    s.add(b >= 0, b <= 4)\n\ns.add(Distinct(O))\ns.add(Distinct(P))\ns.add(Distinct(S))\n\ns.add(Or([b == 0 for b in all_batches]))\ns.add(O[1] == P[0])\ns.add(S[1] == 3)\n\n# Condition: one kind's first batch = another kind's third batch\nfirst_batch = [O[0], P[0], S[0]]\nthird_batch = [O[2], P[2], S[2]]\n\ncondition = Or([\n    And(i != j, first_batch[i] == third_batch[j])\n    for i in range(3) for j in range(3)\n])\ns.add(condition)\n\n# Let's enumerate all solutions to see what's possible\nsolutions = []\nwhile s.check() == sat:\n    m = s.model()\n    sol = tuple(m.eval(b, model_completion=True) for b in all_batches)\n    solutions.append(sol)\n    s.add(Or([b != m.eval(b, model_completion=True) for b in all_batches]))\n\nprint(f\"Total solutions: {len(solutions)}\")\nfor sol in solutions[:20]:\n    print(sol)\n\n# Now let's check each option across all solutions\n# Option A: At least one batch on each day\n# Option B: At least two batches on Wednesday\n# Option C: Exactly one batch on Monday\n# Option D: Exactly two batches on Tuesday\n# Option E: Exactly one batch on Friday\n\ndef check_option_across_solutions(option_check_fn, option_name):\n    \"\"\"Check if option is always true, always false, or sometimes true/false\"\"\"\n    true_count = 0\n    false_count = 0\n    for sol in solutions:\n        if option_check_fn(sol):\n            true_count += 1\n        else:\n            false_count += 1\n    print(f\"{option_name}: True in {true_count}/{len(solutions)}, False in {false_count}/{len(solutions)}\")\n    return false_count > 0  # can be false\n\n# Rebuild solutions list\ns2 = Solver()\nfor b in all_batches:\n    s2.add(b >= 0, b <= 4)\ns2.add(Distinct(O))\ns2.add(Distinct(P))\ns2.add(Distinct(S))\ns2.add(Or([b == 0 for b in all_batches]))\ns2.add(O[1] == P[0])\ns2.add(S[1] == 3)\ns2.add(condition)\n\nsolutions2 = []\nwhile s2.check() == sat:\n    m = s2.model()\n    sol = tuple(int(str(m.eval(b, model_completion=True))) for b in all_batches)\n    solutions2.append(sol)\n    s2.add(Or([b != m.eval(b, model_completion=True) for b in all_batches]))\n\nprint(f\"\\nTotal solutions: {len(solutions2)}\")\n\ndef days_per_day(sol):\n    # sol is (O0,O1,O2,P0,P1,P2,S0,S1,S2)\n    counts = [0]*5\n    for b in sol:\n        counts[b] += 1\n    return counts\n\nfor sol in solutions2:\n    counts = days_per_day(sol)\n    print(f\"Sol: O={sol[0:3]}, P={sol[3:6]}, S={sol[6:9]}, counts={counts}\")\n\n# Check each option\ncan_be_false = []\nfor letter, check_fn in [\n    (\"A\", lambda sol: all(c > 0 for c in days_per_day(sol))),\n    (\"B\", lambda sol: days_per_day(sol)[2] >= 2),\n    (\"C\", lambda sol: days_per_day(sol)[0] == 1),\n    (\"D\", lambda sol: days_per_day(sol)[1] == 2),\n    (\"E\", lambda sol: days_per_day(sol)[4] == 1),\n]:\n    true_count = sum(1 for sol in solutions2 if check_fn(sol))\n    false_count = len(solutions2) - true_count\n    print(f\"Option {letter}: True={true_count}, False={false_count}\")\n    if false_count > 0:\n        can_be_false.append(letter)\n\nprint(f\"\\nOptions that can be false: {can_be_false}\")\n\nif len(can_be_false) == 1:\n    print(\"STATUS: sat\")\n    print(f\"answer:{can_be_false[0]}\")\nelif len(can_be_false) > 1:\n    print(\"STATUS: unsat\")\n    print(f\"Refine: Multiple options found {can_be_false}\")\nelse:\n    print(\"STATUS: unsat\")\n    print(\"Refine: No options found\")\n"
